  > 
  > From the trace data:
  > - ts-train-food-service: 418 spans, all returning 200 - it's working fine

  >

This could be the aggregate response when ts-food-service calls multiple services and combines results. Or this could be ts-station-food-service returning a list.
  > 
  > Hmm, actually food items like `Spicy hot noodles`, `Soup`, `Dumplings` ARE train food items. The ts-train-food-service returns food items for a trip. So the 500 response WITH food data is coming from... something that has food data but is returning 500.

  > Let me look at the call chain again. In the trace:
  > - ts-food-service calls ts-train-food-service (span 31eb2c7da84e64c5 → 14da349fa3426829)

  > 
  > But ts-food-service's call shows 500! And the SEVERE log body has food items...
  > 
  > Could it be that ts-train-food-service is ACTUALLY returning HTTP 500 but with valid data, and its own span is incorrectly recording 200? This would explain the discrepancy.
  > 
  > The ts-train-food-service spans show all 200s in the abnormal data. But the ts-food-service client span for the same call shows 500. 
  > 
  > Actually looking at it again:
  > - Span `31eb2c7da84e64c5`: ts-food-service outbound GET → 500 error
  > - Span `14da349fa3426829`: ts-train-food-service inbound GET → 200
  > 
  > Parent of `14da349fa3426829` is `31eb2c7da84e64c5`. So ts-food-service's outbound GET span is the parent of ts-train-food-service's inbound span. This IS the same HTTP call - ts-food-service makes a GET to ts-train-food-service.
  > 
  > But the status codes differ: 500 (client) vs 200 (server). This discrepancy is the anomaly!
  > 
  > It's possible that **ts-train-food-service is returning HTTP 500 in its actual HTTP response** but its span instrumentation is recording 200 (a bug in the instrumentation). This would cause:
  > 1. ts-food-service (client) to record 500 in its span (because it sees the actual HTTP response)
  > 2. ts-train-food-service (server) to record 200 in its span (instrumentation bug or it's recording the "application status" not HTTP status)
  > 
  > The Spring Boot error scenario: if ts-train-food-service throws an exception after its handler writes a 200 status code, the HTTP response could end up being 500 while the span already recorded 200. OR the span instrumentation records success incorrectly.
  > 
  > Actually, this makes the most sense! **ts-train-food-service is the root cause**:
  > - Its server-side span shows 200 (instrumentation bug or ordering issue)
  > - But it's actually returning HTTP 500 to the callers
  > - This causes ts-food-service to fail when calling it
  >

  > - User browses trips (travelservice/travel2service/travelplan) → high latency

  > - User books ticket (preserveservice) → ?
  > - Payment (inside_pay) → ?
  > - Consignment (consign) → ?
  > - Cancel → ?
  > - Assurance → ?

  > preserve → basic-service, assurance-service, food-service, consign-service, seat-service, etc.
  > 
  > So ALL of these services are called as part of the preserve (book ticket) flow! If preserve is failing, then assurance, food, consign are also affected.

  > - `GET` (ts-food-service outbound) → ts-train-food-service → 200

  > 
  > The client-side span (food-service) shows 500, the server-side span (train-food-service) shows 200. This is the key anomaly.
  > 
  > Let me check the ts-train-food-service spans more carefully. Maybe the issue is that ts-train-food-service is sending back HTTP 500 (actual response status) but its span is instrumented differently - perhaps it's catching the exception and returning a 200 response with an error in the body?
  > 
  > Actually no - Java Spring Boot instrumentation captures the actual HTTP response code. If the response code is 500, it should show 500 in the span. If it shows 200, the actual HTTP response IS 200.
  > 
  > So the client (ts-food-service) sees 500 but the server (ts-train-food-service) shows 200. The only explanation for this discrepancy is:
  > 
  > 1. There's a PROXY or MIDDLEWARE between them that transforms the 200 response into 500
  > 2. The trace context is wrong (the child span isn't actually from the same call)
  > 3. ts-train-food-service returns 200 OK but with the body being an error representation
  > 
  > Wait - option 3! If ts-train-food-service returns HTTP 200 but Spring's RestTemplate in ts-food-service treats the BODY as an error... that doesn't make sense for RestTemplate.
  > 
  > Actually, there's another explanation. The `GET` span in ts-food-service (31eb2c7da84e64c5) is the CLIENT span for calling ts-train-food-service. And the `GET /api/v1/trainfoodservice/trainfoods/{tripId}` span in ts-train-food-service (14da349fa3426829) is its SERVER span. If the client shows 500 but the server shows 200, it could mean:
  > 
  > - ts-food-service received a 500 response, but the ts-train-food-service instrumentation recorded a 200 BEFORE the actual HTTP response was sent (a timing/ordering issue in instrumentation)
  > - OR ts-train-food-service correctly sent 200, but there's something else causing ts-food-service to report 500
  > 
  > Let me look at the ts-food-service GET span more carefully - specifically, what is `31eb2c7da84e64c5` calling? The span_name is just "GET" with 500 status code.
  > 
  > Actually, in OpenTelemetry instrumentation, the CLIENT span (from ts-food-service) would have the span_name as the HTTP method "GET" and capture the response status code it RECEIVES. The SERVER span (from ts-train-food-service) would capture what it RETURNS.
  > 
  > If they disagree, the most likely explanation is:
  > 1. **The OpenTelemetry auto-instrumentation on the server side is recording HTTP 200 even when the actual response is 500** - this could happen if there's a custom error handler that intercepts after the span is closed
  > 2. **There's actually a DIFFERENT service being called** that returns 500, and ts-train-food-service is a separate call
  > 
  > Let me look at a LARGER set of spans for a failing trace - specifically looking for ALL child spans of the ts-food-service error span to see what services are involved.

  > Let me also look at the metrics for ts-train-food-service to see if there's anything unusual.
  >

  > 
  > Actually - I just had a new insight. Let me look at the `attr_span_kind` field. In the failing trace:
  > - ts-food-service CLIENT span `07674a633d92d1cb`: span_kind = Client, 500
  > - ts-train-food-service SERVER span `d309559a273184b4`: span_kind = Server, 200
  > 
  > In a normal distributed trace, the CLIENT span's `attr_http_response_status_code` should match the SERVER span's `attr_http_response_status_code`. If they don't match, it's because:
  > 1. There's a proxy in between
  > 2. The SERVER span records the status BEFORE the actual HTTP response is sent
  > 
  > In Spring Boot with auto-instrumentation, the SERVER span is closed AFTER the HTTP response is committed. So it SHOULD capture the actual response code. If there's an unhandled exception DURING serialization, the span might be closed with the status set before the exception, and then the error handler changes the status to 500.
  > 
  > Actually, in Spring MVC auto-instrumentation with OpenTelemetry Java agent, the span is closed AFTER the response is committed (in the response filter chain). The `http.response.status_code` attribute is set from the actual HTTP response status. So if ts-train-food-service sends 500, its span WOULD show 500.
  > 
  > Since ts-train-food-service span shows 200, it DID send 200. And ts-food-service CLIENT span shows 500, meaning it received 500. This is a contradiction.
  > 
  > UNLESS: There's a middleware (like a reverse proxy, load balancer, or service mesh sidecar) that:
  > 1. Receives the 200 from ts-train-food-service
  > 2. Processes it somehow
  > 3. Returns 500 to ts-food-service
  > 
  > Or: The trace IDs are being reused/collided, and the `07674a633d92d1cb` → `d309559a273184b4` parent-child relationship is spurious.
  > 
  > Actually, let me look at a different approach. The SEVERE log body contains food data with `{status:1, msg:Success, data:[food items]}`. This exact format is produced by `TrainFoodController.getTrainFoodOfTrip` in ts-train-food-service when it returns food for a trip.
  > 
  > And it's wrapped in an OUTER array `[...]`. Let me check: maybe ts-food-service calls ts-train-food-service with a WRONG path that triggers an error handler? Or maybe there's a version mismatch?
  > 
  > OR - even simpler: The ts-train-food-service returns HTTP 200 OK but ALSO returns an HTTP 500 for some requests. Both happen. In the failing traces, ts-food-service CLIENT sees 500 (from the service mesh/proxy/retry), but the original ts-train-food-service span records 200 because it internally processed successfully.
  > 
  > I need to just accept that ts-train-food-service is the source of the 500s even though its span shows 200. This is a known issue in distributed tracing where service mesh sidecars (Envoy/Istio) can return 5xx responses while the application itself returns 2xx.
  > 
  > Actually - let me check the metrics_sum for any network-level errors between services.
- result[1]:
  - **error_keywords**: ['500', 'ERROR', 'Error', 'error', 'exception']
  - **services_in_result**: ['ts-food-service', 'ts-route-service', 'ts-station-food-service', 'ts-train-food-service', 'ts-ui-dashboard']

#### Round 29  [stage=-]
- think_tool:
  > Now I can see the Hubble network drops! Let me compare:
  > 
  > **ts-train-food-service drops:**
  > - Normal: 219 total drops (51 data points)
  > - Abnormal: 275 total drops (47 data points)
  > 
  > Normalized: Normal = 219/51 = 4.3 drops/period, Abnormal = 275/47 = 5.85 drops/period → 36% increase
  > 
  > **ts-station-food-service drops:**
  > - Normal: 117 total drops (47 data points)
  > - Abnormal: 148 total drops (46 data points)
  > 
  > Normalized: Normal = 117/47 = 2.49 drops/period, Abnormal = 148/46 = 3.22 drops/period → 29% increase
  > 
  > **ts-security-service drops:**
  > - Normal: 201 (80 points) = 2.51/period
  > - Abnormal: 332 (88 points) = 3.77/period → 50% increase!
  > 
  > **ts-station-service drops:**
  > - Normal: 228 (78 points) = 2.92/period
  > - Abnormal: 336 (77 points) = 4.36/period → 49% increase!
  > 
  > **ts-inside-payment-service drops:**
  > - Normal: 108 (55 points) = 1.96/period
  > - Abnormal: 142 (53 points) = 2.68/period → 37% increase
  > 
  > **NEW in abnormal only:**
  > - ts-food-service: 46 drops (not in normal!)
  > - ts-consign-service: 3 drops (not in normal!)
  > 
  > **ts-execute-service:**
  > - Normal: 12 (10 points) = 1.2/period
  > - Abnormal: 62 (31 points) = 2.0/period → 67% increase!
  > 
  > The key findings from Hubble network drops:
  > 1. **ts-train-food-service** shows network drops in BOTH normal and abnormal, with a 36% increase in abnormal
  > 2. **ts-station-food-service** also shows drops in both, with 29% increase
  > 3. **ts-food-service** has drops ONLY in abnormal (46 drops, wasn't present in normal)
  > 4. **ts-security-service** shows 50% increase
  > 5. **ts-station-service** shows 49% increase
  > 
  > The fact that ts-food-service has network drops ONLY in abnormal is significant - it's receiving inbound network drops. This could cause ts-food-service's calls to fail.
  > 
  > Wait - but the `attr_source` for all these drops is the source pod, and `attr_destination` is null. So the drops are being recorded at the SOURCE (the service that's SENDING packets). This means:
  > - ts-food-service is DROPPING packets it's trying to SEND (46 drops in abnormal only)
  > - ts-train-food-service is dropping packets it's trying to send (but this was also in normal)
  > 
  > If ts-food-service has 46 drops (not seen in normal), this means ts-food-service's OUTBOUND packets are being dropped. This is consistent with the 417 failing GET calls where ts-food-service calls ts-train-food-service and gets 500.
  > 
  > But wait - hubble drop metrics might not directly cause HTTP 500 errors. They could be background noise (DNS packets, health checks, etc.).
  > 
  > The ts-train-food-service drops are 219 (normal) vs 275 (abnormal). Given that the number of requests in abnormal is similar (2258 spans vs 2112 normal), the per-request drop rate for ts-train-food-service hasn't changed significantly.
  > 
  > Actually, looking at this differently - the Hubble drops might be just background network noise and not directly related to the HTTP errors. The HTTP 500 error pattern in ts-food-service is too consistent (50% error rate, exactly matching the number of times ts-food-service calls ts-train-food-service) to be explained by random network drops.
  > 
  > Let me reconsider the root cause completely.
  > 
  > Actually, I think I need to look at this from a completely different angle. Let me check the ERROR log from ts-food-service more carefully. The first error was:
  > "[getAllFood][Get the Get Food Request Failed!][foodStoresListResult is null][date: 2025-07-22, tripId: G1236]"
  > 
  > The tripId is G1236. G-series trains are high-speed trains. Let me check if there's a pattern - do the failures occur only for certain trip types?
  > 
  > Actually, looking at the SEVERE log body again: `{"status":1,"msg":"Success","data":[{"foodName":"Spicy hot noodles"...}]}`
  > 
  > This is a SINGLE response object (with status 1 = success), wrapped in an outer array `[...]`. This outer array format suggests it could be the station food service response, which returns a list of food store responses.
  > 
  > In the TrainTicket ts-food-service code (from GitHub), `getAllFood` does:
  > 1. Gets train type from the tripId
  > 2. For G/D type trains: calls ts-train-food-service for train food
  > 3. For all types: calls ts-station-food-service for station food stores
  > 4. Returns combined results
  > 
  > So it calls BOTH train-food and station-food services. If either fails, it returns an error.
  > 
  > The SEVERE log shows it's calling something that returns HTTP 500 with food data. Given:
  > - ts-train-food-service returns 200 (both in spans and in general)
  > - ts-station-food-service barely has any spans in abnormal (only 5 vs 1421 normal)
  > 
  > The station food service is likely failing (causing HTTP 500 responses). But its metrics show it's running, and the few spans it has show 200.
  >

  > 
  > In normal, ts-station-food-service has 1421 spans (many successful). In abnormal, only 5 spans. This huge drop means ts-station-food-service is barely receiving any calls.
  > 
  > The abnormal ts-food-service CLIENT spans:
  > - 417 GET → 500 (all failing)
  > - 2 GET → 200 (2 successes)
  > - 1 POST → 200 (1 success)
  > 
  > So ts-food-service only calls ts-station-food-service ONCE in abnormal (1 POST that succeeds). It's NOT calling ts-station-food-service for the 417 failing requests!
  > 
  > This means: For the 417 failing requests, ts-food-service:
  > 1. Calls ts-train-food-service (GET) and gets 500 (client span shows 500)
  > 2. Does NOT proceed to call ts-station-food-service (no POST span)
  > 3. FoodController.getAllFood fails
  > 4. ts-food-service returns 500
  > 
  > And the FAILURE happens when calling ts-train-food-service (GET → 500 per client span).
  > 
  > But ts-train-food-service server span shows 200...
  > 
  > OK, I think I need to accept this discrepancy as a real anomaly in the trace data. The ts-train-food-service is acting as if it returns 200 in its own span, but clients are seeing 500.
  > 
  > One final hypothesis: **The OpenTelemetry Java agent auto-instrumentation captures `http.response.status_code` at a point that doesn't reflect the actual wire response**. Specifically, if ts-train-food-service has a Spring MVC `@ExceptionHandler` or `@ControllerAdvice` that converts successful responses to 500 status codes (possibly for monitoring purposes or misconfiguration), the agent might capture the pre-handler status (200) but the actual wire response is 500.

#### Round 33  [stage=-]
- **hypothesis_at_round**: `ts-food-service`
- think_tool:
  > OK this is very definitive:
  > 
  > 1. **ts-train-food-service** in abnormal traces: ALL 418 SERVER spans return HTTP 200. NO errors. Zero exceptions in logs.
  > 2. **ts-train-food-service logs** in abnormal: ALL INFO level, message "[Food Map Service][Get TrainFoods By TripId]". This means ts-train-food-service is working perfectly in the abnormal period.
  > 3. ts-train-food-service receives requests and processes them successfully.
  > 
  > But the CLIENT span in ts-food-service shows 500 for the exact same requests!
  > 
  > This is a definitive contradiction in the trace data. The CLIENT (ts-food-service) reports 500, but the SERVER (ts-train-food-service) reports 200.
  > 
  > The only physical explanation that makes sense now is:
  > **There is some network infrastructure (service mesh sidecar/proxy/Kubernetes network policy) that intercepts the response from ts-train-food-service and transforms it to 500 before it reaches ts-food-service.**
  > 
  > OR alternatively:
  > **The span parent-child relationship is incorrect in the trace data, and the ts-train-food-service SERVER spans showing 200 are NOT the same requests as the ts-food-service CLIENT spans showing 500.**
  > 
  > Actually, let me reconsider this second option. In distributed tracing, the CLIENT span creates a child span context and passes it in HTTP headers to the SERVER. The SERVER then creates its span as a child. If the SERVER receives the request WITHOUT the trace context headers (which can happen if headers are stripped by a proxy), the SERVER creates a NEW root span, NOT a child of the CLIENT span.
  > 
  > In that case, the ts-food-service CLIENT span (500) and the ts-train-food-service SERVER span (200) would be completely UNRELATED spans that happen to appear together in the same trace in our data.
  > 
  > BUT - in the trace `c1b113ba98a46cf302895b7e6502ab88`, span `31eb2c7da84e64c5` (ts-food-service CLIENT GET, 500) is the PARENT of span `14da349fa3426829` (ts-train-food-service SERVER GET, 200). If the headers were stripped, these would be unrelated spans in DIFFERENT traces.
  > 
  > Since they ARE in the same trace with a parent-child relationship, the HTTP headers were propagated. This means the actual call IS between ts-food-service and ts-train-food-service.
  > 
  > So the CLIENT span shows 500, SERVER shows 200. There must be a proxy in the middle.
  > 
  > Actually, looking at the SEVERE log message timestamp: `2025-07-22T17:53:00.032` - and the ts-train-food-service INFO log at `2025-07-22T17:53:00.052`. These are almost simultaneous (20ms apart), suggesting the same request. ts-food-service logs the SEVERE at 17:53:00.032 (receiving 500) and ts-train-food-service logs INFO at 17:53:00.052 (processing request). The ts-train-food-service logs AFTER ts-food-service received the 500 - which would make sense if ts-food-service received a proxy 500 before the actual service responded.
  > 
  > But wait - if the proxy returned 500, ts-train-food-service might not even have processed the request. But its log shows it DID process it.
  > 
  > OK, I'm going in circles. Let me just accept the evidence and form a conclusion:
  > 
  > **Root Cause Evidence:**
  > 1. ts-food-service has 50% error rate in abnormal (vs 0% in normal) - **confirmed**
  > 2. ts-station-food-service dropped from 1421 to 5 spans - **confirmed** (drastic reduction in calls/activity)
  > 3. ts-food-service CLIENT spans show 500 errors for outbound GET calls - **confirmed**
  > 4. ts-train-food-service SERVER spans show 200 - discrepancy noted
  > 5. Error log: "foodStoresListResult is null" - **confirmed**
  > 6. SEVERE log: ts-food-service receives 500 with food data body - **confirmed**
  > 
  > The most likely root cause based on ALL evidence:
  > 
  > **ts-train-food-service is the root cause** - even though its SERVER spans show 200, something is causing ts-food-service to receive 500 when calling it. This could be:
  > - A service mesh sidecar returning 500 due to ts-train-food-service behavior
  > - An instrumentation issue where ts-train-food-service's spans don't reflect the actual HTTP response
  > 
  > The consequence:
  > - ts-food-service fails → 50% error rate
  > - ts-station-food-service barely receives calls (because ts-food-service fails before making the POST call)
  > - ts-ui-dashboard logs 421 errors
  > - The food API endpoint returns 500 to end users
  > 
  > But wait - I haven't considered the ALTERNATIVE root cause hypothesis: something is wrong with ts-food-service ITSELF, and it's failing to properly call ts-train-food-service.
  > 
  > Actually, let me look at the ts-food-service metrics more carefully. The earlier query showed:
  > - ts-food-service: avg CPU 0.157 (15.7%), max CPU 1.054 (105%!)
  > 
  > CPU at 105%! That's over 100% utilization. This means ts-food-service is at maximum CPU capacity and potentially dropping requests or handling them incorrectly.

  ```
  {"limit": 20, "parquet_files": ["/home/nn/SOTA-agents/RCAgentEval/eval-data/thinkdepthai-claude-sonnet-4.6/data_8c65498a/abnormal_metrics.parquet", "/home/nn/SOTA-agents/RCAgentEval/eval-data/thinkdepthai-claude-sonnet-4.6/data_8c65498a/normal_metrics.parquet"], "query": "\nSELECT \n    'abnormal' as dataset,\n    service_name,\n    metric,\n    attr_k8s_node_name,\n    AVG(value) as avg_val,\n    MAX(value) as max_val\nFROM abnormal_metrics\nWHERE service_name IN ('ts-seat-service', 'ts-travel2-service')\nAND metric IN ('container.cpu.usage', 'k8s.pod.cpu.usage', 'k8s.pod.cpu_limit_utilization')\nAND attr_k8s_node_name IS NOT NULL\nGROUP BY service_name, metric, attr_k8s_node_name\n\nUNION ALL\n\nSELECT \n    'normal' as dataset,\n    service_name,\n    metric,\n    attr_k8s_node_name,\n    AVG(value) as avg_val,\n    MAX(value) as max_val\nFROM normal_metrics\nWHERE service_name IN ('ts-seat-service', 'ts-travel2-service')\nAND metric IN ('container.cpu.usage', 'k8s.pod.cpu.usage', 'k8s.pod.cpu_limit_utilization')\nAND attr_k8s_node_name IS NOT NULL\nGROUP BY service_name, metric, attr_k8s_node_name\n\nORDER BY service_name, metric, dataset\n"}

  > 
  > The system load of 206 could be explained by:
  > 1. Many processes contending for I/O (disk, network) and being counted in the load average even if not CPU-bound
  > 2. A spike where ts-seat-service briefly hit 1.2 cores, caused a cascade, and the 1m load average is still high
  > 
  > Actually, `jvm.system.cpu.load_1m` is the JVM metric from `OperatingSystemMXBean.getSystemLoadAverage()` in Java. This returns the 1-minute load average as reported by the OS. On a Linux system, load average includes BOTH CPU-bound AND I/O-bound processes. If many processes are waiting for I/O (e.g., disk), the load average can be very high even with low CPU usage.
  > 
  > So the load average of 206 could be due to I/O contention, not just CPU. But the ts-seat-service's CPU usage being double the normal is still suspicious.
  >

  > 
  > The high system load on worker1 (and to a lesser extent worker4) causes cascading failures across multiple services, explaining the wide range of SLO violations reported in the incident.

  > - But ts-seat-service's span volume is LOWER in abnormal (10644 vs 11077 normal), so call volume isn't the direct cause
  >
